### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-09-30
Since it is already October for half the world, I thought I'd post the October thread!

Rules:

[LIST=1]
[*]                              Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
[*] If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
[*] Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
[*] The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
[*]  The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
[*]  Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
[*]  To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:
[/LIST]
[INDENT] Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
[/INDENT]**Important Note: **Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2009-10-01
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> and is that vimperator you're using?
Yup. My own colors are used, putting them here in the event they're wanted.
```

hi Hint      font-family: terminus; font-size: 11px; font-weight: normal; color: lightyellow; background-color: #333; border-color: ButtonShadow; border-width: 0px; border-style: solid; padding: 0px 5px;
 
hi HintElem    background-color: #007FA3;    color: #333;
hi HintActive    background-color: #007FA3;  color: white;
 
hi StatusLine     color: #007FA3;  background: #333;  font-family: terminus; font-weight: normal; font-size: 11pt;

hi CmdLine  font-family: terminus; font-size: 11px; padding: 1px;

hi Normal     color: LightYellow;  background: #333;  font-family: terminus; font-size: 11pt;
hi InfoMsg    color: LightYellow;  background: #333;  font-family: terminus; font-size: 11pt;
hi ModeMsg    color: LightYellow;  background: #333;  font-family: terminus; font-size: 11pt;
hi MoreMsg    color: LimeGreen;  background: #333;
hi LineNr    color: #007FA3;  background: #333;  font-family: terminus; font-size: 11pt;
hi Question    color: Yellow;    background: #333;  font-family: terminus; font-size: 11pt;
hi WarningMsg    color: #007FA3;  background: #333;  font-family: terminus; font-size: 11pt;
hi NonText     background: #333;
hi Null      color: CornflowerBlue;
hi Tag      color: CornflowerBlue;
 
hi CompTitle    color: #007FA3;    background: #333;  font-family: terminus; font-weight: bold;
hi CompItem[selected]  font-family: terminus; color: #007FA3;  background: #333;
hi CompDesc    font-family: terminus; color: #007FA3;
hi Gradient     height: 1px; margin-bottom: -1px; margin-top -1px; background-color: #333;
hi GradientRight  background-color: #333;
hi GradientLeft   background-color: #00B1Ed
 
hi Title    font-family: terminus; color: white;
hi Indicator    font-family: terminus; color: DodgerBlue;
hi String    font-family: terminus; color: Orchid;
hi Number    font-family: terminus; color: Orchid;
hi Object    font-family: terminus; color: Khaki;
hi Function    font-family: terminus; color: SkyBlue;
hi URL      font-family: terminus; color: LightGreen;
 
hi TabNumber    color: black; font-family: terminus; font-weight: bold; font-size: 11pt;
 
style -name tab chrome://* <<EOM
#content { background-color: #ccc; } /* tabbar */
.tabs-alltabs-button { padding: 0 !important; }
.tabs-container > stack { display: none; } /* remove tab selection menu 
*/
/*.tabs-container .box-inherit.scrollbox-innerbox { border-bottom: 1px 
solid #404040; } /* tab bar position: top */
.tabs-container scrollbox {
  background-color: #adadad;
  border-bottom: 1px solid #333;
}
.tabbrowser-tab {
  -moz-apperance: none !important;
  margin: 0 !important;
  padding: 0 !important;
  -moz-border-radius-topleft: 0 !important;
  -moz-border-radius-topright: 0 !important;
  -moz-border-radius-bottomright: 0 !important;
  -moz-border-radius-bottomleft: 0 !important;
  border-bottom: 1px solid #000 !important;
  background-image: none !important;
  background-color: #ff69b4 !important;
  text-align: left !important;
}
.tabbrowser-tab[selected=false] { background: #999 !important; }
.tabbrowser-tab[selected=true] .tab-text { color: #007FA3 !important; }
.tab-icon-image { margin-bottom: -4px; }
.tab-image-left,
.tab-image-middle,
.tab-image-right {
  background-image: none !important;
}
EOM
 
style -name statusbar chrome://* <<EOM
#status-bar statusbarpanel { padding: 0 1px !important; }
statusbarpanel > * { margin: 0 !important; padding: 0 !important; }
EOM


```

### Post by Lightstar on 2009-10-01
> **ihermit said:**
> What is Greenlife emerald view? and what's that game you're playing?

> **etnlIcarus said:**
> IIRC, Greenlife is a client for Second Life. Evidentially, he's playing Second Life, with an Okami Amaterasu avatar.

Oooo you are good!   That's exactly it.
Greenlife Emerald has alot more features compared to the normal viewer.

It's an online world, most use it for chatting, but there's also alot of avatar customization, 3D building (secondlife has it's own 3D building engine type of thing).  There's in-world games.  Everything in the world is made by it's users.  It's more like a mini-platform than a 3D chat really.  It's free, feel free to try it.  [http://www.secondlife.com](http://www.secondlife.com)

### Post by Megrimn on 2009-10-01
Using the 'wild mint' theme with the aurora gtk.  Nabbed those off my linux mint install on a different computer.  I love how it's a dark theme, yet you can still read everything clearly (i.e. audacity).  

A friend of mine sent me the wallpaper.  I don't remember if he did it himself or not, but it was made using a fractal plugin in photoshop.  Wish gimp had a fractal plugin that worked like that.

Icon theme is 'royal blue' from gnome-look.org, but I tweaked it quite a bit.  several of the icons give that away.


oh, and i use winamp under wine to play adx files. full version didn't work, but the lite version is perfect.

### Post by rjmdomingo2003 on 2009-10-01
> **Sarai the Geek said:**
> Neat conky! Can you indulge my laziness and post the config?
Sure.

rings.lua (modified from ali's script)
```
--[[
Ring Meters by londonali1010 (2009)

This script draws percentage meters as rings. It is fully customisable; all options are described in the script.

IMPORTANT: if you are using the 'cpu' function, it will cause a segmentation fault if it tries to draw a ring straight away. The if statement on line 129 uses a delay to make sure that this doesn't happen. It calculates the length of the delay by the number of updates since Conky started. Generally, a value of 5s is long enough, so if you update Conky every 1s, use update_num>5 in that if statement (the default). If you only update Conky every 2s, you should change it to update_num>3; conversely if you update Conky every 0.5s, you should use update_num>10. ALSO, if you change your Conky, is it best to use "killall conky; conky" to update it, otherwise the update_num will not be reset and you will get an error.

To call this script in Conky, use the following (assuming that you save this script to ~/scripts/rings.lua):
	lua_load ~/scripts/rings.lua
	lua_draw_hook_pre ring_stats
	
Changelog:
+ v1.1 -- Added options for the starting angle of the rings, and added the "max" variable, to allow for variables that output a numerical value rather than a percentage (29.09.2009)
+ v1.0 -- Original release (28.09.2009)
]]

settings_table = {
	{
		-- Edit this table to customise your rings.
		-- You can create more rings simply by adding more elements to settings_table.
		-- "name" is the type of stat to display; you can choose from 'cpu', 'memperc', 'fs_used_perc', 'battery_used_perc'.
		name='cpu',
		-- "arg" is the argument to the stat type, e.g. if in Conky you would write ${cpu cpu0}, 'cpu0' would be the argument. If you would not use an argument in the Conky variable, use ''.
		arg='cpu0',
		-- "max" is the maximum value of the ring. If the Conky variable outputs a percentage, use 100.
		max=100,
		-- "bg_colour" is the colour of the base ring.
		bg_colour=0xffffff,
		-- "bg_alpha" is the alpha value of the base ring.
		bg_alpha=0.1,
		-- "fg_colour" is the colour of the indicator part of the ring.
		fg_colour=0xffffff,
		-- "fg_alpha" is the alpha value of the indicator part of the ring.
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		-- "x" and "y" are the x and y coordinates of the centre of the ring, relative to the top left corner of the Conky window.
		x=1101, y=282,
		-- "radius" is the radius of the ring.
		radius=27.4,
		-- "thickness" is the thickness of the ring, centred around the radius.
		thickness=5,
		-- "angle" is the starting angle of the ring, in degrees, clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative.
		angle=-90
	},
	{
		name='cpu',
		arg='cpu1',
		max=100,
		bg_colour=0xffffff,
		bg_alpha=0.1,
		fg_colour=0xffffff,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=1101, y=282,
		radius=32.2,
		thickness=5,
		angle=-90
	},
	{
		name='fs_used_perc',
		arg='/home/melski',
		max=100,
		bg_colour=0xffffff,
		bg_alpha=0.1,
		fg_colour=0xffffff,
		fg_alpha=0.5,
		x=1101, y=282,
		radius=10,
		thickness=20,
		angle=-90
	},
	{
		name='battery_percent',
		arg='BAT1',
		max=100,
		bg_colour=0xffffff,
		bg_alpha=0.1,
		fg_colour=0xffffff,
		fg_alpha=1,
		x=1101, y=282,
		radius=22.4,
		thickness=5,
		angle=-90
	},
}

require 'cairo'

function rgb_to_r_g_b(colour,alpha)
	return ((colour / 0x10000) % 0x100) / 255., ((colour / 0x100) % 0x100) / 255., (colour % 0x100) / 255., alpha
end

function draw_ring(t, pt)
	if conky_window==nil then return end
	local w,h=conky_window.width,conky_window.height
	local cs=cairo_xlib_surface_create(conky_window.display,conky_window.drawable,conky_window.visual,w,h)
	
	cr=cairo_create(cs)
	
	local xc,yc,ring_r,ring_w,angle=pt['x'],pt['y'],pt['radius'],pt['thickness'],pt['angle']
	local bgc, bga, fgc, fga=pt['bg_colour'], pt['bg_alpha'], pt['fg_colour'], pt['fg_alpha']

	local angle_0=angle*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
	local t_arc=t*2*math.pi

	-- Draw background ring

	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,ring_r,0,2*math.pi)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(bgc,bga))
	cairo_set_line_width(cr,ring_w)
	cairo_stroke(cr)
	
	-- Draw indicator ring

	cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,ring_r,angle_0,angle_0+t_arc)
	cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(fgc,fga))
	cairo_stroke(cr)		
	
	cairo_destroy(cr)
	cr = nil
end

function conky_cairo_cleanup()
	cairo_surface_destroy(cs)
	cs = nil
end

function conky_ring_stats()
	local function setup_rings(pt)
		local str=''
		local value=0
		
		str=string.format('${%s %s}',pt['name'],pt['arg'])
		if pcall(conky_parse,str) then
			str = conky_parse(str)
		else str='0'
		end
		
		value=tonumber(str)
		pct=value/pt['max']
		
		draw_ring(pct,pt)
	end
	
	-- Check that Conky has been running for at least 5s
	
	local updates=conky_parse('${updates}')
	update_num=tonumber(updates)
	
	if update_num>5 then
		for i in pairs(settings_table) do
			setup_rings(settings_table[i])
		end
	end
end
```

and the conkyrc
```
use_xft yes
xftfont Gill Sans MT Light:size=22.24
minimum_size 160 800
maximum_width 1200
update_interval 2
total_run_times 0
own_window no
own_window_transparent no
own_window_type widget
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager 
double_buffer yes
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
stippled_borders 0
border_margin 2
border_width 1
default_color 3b3b3b
#default_shade_color white
#default_outline_color black
own_window_colour 08090a
#alignment top_left
alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right
gap_x 70
gap_y 68
no_buffers yes
uppercase yes
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale yes
use_spacer yes
short_units yes
imlib_cache_size 0
lua_load ~/documents/rings.lua
lua_draw_hook_pre ring_stats

TEXT
D${offset -1}X${offset -2}B${offset -1}${font Gill Sans MT Light:bold:pixelsize=28}${color 808a93}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c1}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c2}${offset -2}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c3}${offset -2}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c4}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c5}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c6}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c7}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c8}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c9}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c10}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c11}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c12}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c13}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c14}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c15}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c16}${offset -3}${execi 1800 conkyForecast --location=AEXX0004 --datatype=CC | cut -c17}${font}${color}

${image /home/melski/images/line.png -s 1x210 -p 52,0}

### Post by misfitpierce on 2009-10-02
Yes you save some ram using gnome's natural compositing engine but... you lose the effects and the difference is only around 20MB which is not much unless you are on a medievil machine!

---

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-10-02
> **SomeGuyDude said:**
> ...it's 1%. How can that POSSIBLY matter to you? Have you ever been sitting there trying to, I don't know, render sixteen videos at once and gone "my god if I only had one more free percent of CPU I'd be able to do this!!!"

---

### Post by credobyte on 2009-10-02
> **misfitpierce said:**
> Yes you save some ram using gnome's natural compositing engine but... you lose the effects and the difference is only around 20MB which is not much unless you are on a medievil machine!

You loose the response time, not RAM.

---

### Post by misfitpierce on 2009-10-02
> **Sarai the Geek said:**
> That's *not* the point. The point is that compared to a lot of window managers, it's not light. That was all I said.

That is indeed a true observation, but if you are able to run Gnome or KDE it does not hurt much to run Compiz as it only takes about another 20MB of ram or so... But yes if limited on ram then Compiz does make the environment heavier and should not be used.

---

### Post by misfitpierce on 2009-10-02
> **credobyte said:**
> You loose the response time, not RAM.

I understand that. It is not a huge difference though really. But like I said if limited on hardware I would just enable the natural Gnome compositing engine which can be done inside gconf-editor under gnome section... Can select enable compositing which is faster compositing without effects loading against the cpu and ram, but im going to end this since this is desktop screenshot thread and not a thread about whether or not we should use compiz etc!

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-10-03
> **Sarai the Geek said:**
> Doesn't using compiz with it sort of defeat the point? I mean, it's supposed to be lightweight and fast, but compiz is pretty heavy...

> **Sarai the Geek said:**
> Not compared to some other compositing window managers. Consider the screenshot above, compiz is using 1% of that guy's cpu. While that may not be a lot, I use xcompmgr and it doesn't even show up in top.

> **Sarai the Geek said:**
> That's *not* the point. The point is that compared to a lot of window managers, it's not light. That was all I said.

You point seems to keep changing. First it's heavy, then it's heavy compared to 'other compositing WMs', then it's heavy compared to other WMs.

> **koleoptero said:**
> I'd like to say something on the compiz thing here too. Since xfce already supports compositing why use compiz? for the extra bling? For the shadows under the windows and menus and the transparencies it's just as good though.
- Full screen zoom.
- Expo for workspace management.
- Window Rules to force window sizes/behaviour.
- Resize Info to help me resize windows specifically.
- Scale for improved window picking.
- Window previews to again improve window picking.
- Ring switcher to again improve window picking.
- Resize overlays to make window resizing smooth.
- More decorator button options.

It's well worth the 5mb jump in RAM usage (20mb - the 15mb xfwm would use) and the couple of bugs it introduces.

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-10-05

also... the rgb part works for me.. but the **a** doesn't! i have Dust, Darkroom and gtk2-engine-murrine installed! D; no transparency =[

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-10-05
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> You're using Ubuntu right? It's designed for Ubuntu. Check by applying my theme, and go to System Monitor. If that window isn't transparent then I don't know.

I have *never* heard of a GTK theme that was specially programmed for one distribution.  

Your "theme" is nothing more than an index.theme file:

```
[Desktop Entry]
Name=Fusion Reborn
Type=X-GNOME-Metatheme
Comment=A Fusion of Dust and Dark Room.\n\nBy Tipped OuT.

[X-GNOME-Metatheme]
GtkTheme=DarkRoom
MetacityTheme=Dust
IconTheme=erectus
GtkColorScheme=fg_color:#ffffffffffff,bg_color:#343433333030,text_color:#ffffffffffff,base_color:#4a524a524a52,selected_fg_color:#ffffffffffff,selected_bg_color:#f3f366660000,tooltip_fg_color:#ffffffffffff,tooltip_bg_color:#343433333030
CursorTheme=default
CursorSize=18
BackgroundImage=/home/yakeem/Firefox_wallpaper.png
```

As long as you are running a distribution that uses Gnome and you have Dust and DarkRoom installed, you should be able to use this theme.

RGBA using the Murrine engine is only supported by a certain number of applications.  There is a full list of supported applications here:  [http://www.cimitan.com/murrine/rgba-support/list](http://www.cimitan.com/murrine/rgba-support/list)

Some of them do RGBA automatically, like gnome-system-monitor.  Others require patches.

---

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-10-05

Your "theme" is nothing more than an index.theme file:

```

```

As long as you are running a distribution that uses Gnome and you have Dust and DarkRoom installed, you should be able to use this theme.

RGBA using the Murrine engine is only supported by a certain number of applications.  There is a full list of supported applications here:  [http://www.cimitan.com/murrine/rgba-support/list](http://www.cimitan.com/murrine/rgba-support/list)

Some of them do RGBA automatically, like gnome-system-monitor.  Others require patches.

Yes I know, but I made this theme in Ubuntu, for Dark Room and Dust. Some people have problems on other distribution becuase it's not actual theme. Just a file that tells what colors and combination of themes to use.

And the rest of the stuff you're talking about I already knew awhile ago.

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-10-07
> **vishzilla said:**
> Nitrogen looks cool. I heard Nitrogen and Oxygen are merged into one project w/ Oxygen getting the bling from Nitrogen
For awhile I was maintaining a Nitrogen package for Debian unstable, and upstream informed the Debian KDE team that Nitrogen would be included with KDE starting with 4.4. I never heard anything about a merger though.

### Post by meho_r on 2009-10-07
Here's the result of my fiddling with Appearance window :) Plain desktop and couple of apps. Still experimenting with fonts and icons though.

[[IMG]http://img14.imageshack.us/img14/1394/screenshot001dn.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img14.imageshack.us/i/screenshot001dn.jpg/) [[IMG]http://img44.imageshack.us/img44/8550/screenshot002bn.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img44.imageshack.us/i/screenshot002bn.jpg/) [[IMG]http://img14.imageshack.us/img14/3097/screenshot003bk.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img14.imageshack.us/i/screenshot003bk.jpg/) [[IMG]http://img14.imageshack.us/img14/9640/screenshot004qe.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img14.imageshack.us/i/screenshot004qe.jpg/)

Here are infos:
- Theme is [Mirav2](http://sen7.deviantart.com/art/Mira-100077120) (package contains Mira 0.5 and Mirav2 themes and GDM)
- Icons are [Dust Karmic](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Dust+Karmic+Iconset+by+mickyz?content=106084) (although [Meliae Dust](http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Meliae-Dust?content=93759) will do too)
- Font is fantastic [Museo](http://www.josbuivenga.demon.nl/museo.html)
- Wallpaper is "Artistic-Colors-71265" (can't recall from where I got it, but it can be found [here](http://zachandbritz.com/bgs/Artistic-Colors-71265.jpg))
- Cactus-swinging-guy can be found on Digg. Probably. :D

### Post by PurposeOfReason on 2009-10-07
> **OpenGuard said:**
> What tiling WM you are using ( Wmii, Awesome, ... ) ? Does it's defaults look pretty much the same as in your screenshot ( colors, borders, spaces, ... ) ?

### Post by DjBones on 2009-10-11
If anybody remembers my last desktop, they'll definitely notice I'm following a pattern haha.  I started using vimperator, and gotta say, it's wicked awesome; the hint system is worth it alone.  I posted the wallpaper too, in case anybody likes it, I took the "Blue Class" wallpaper by basstar on deviantart, then inverted and desaturated it.  Gotta have that gray!

I'm using gnome, so I kinda hacked it together to be as minimal as possible.  Moved the panel to the left side with a 0 pixel width on autohide and changed the window borders to have a 1 pixel outline.  Then xbindkeys takes care of the rest.  I'm really happy with it actually, I've used tilers before, but gnome provides a lot of neat little functionalities that are nice to have.  Running Debian Lenny.

### Post by tehkain on 2009-10-12
> **tibil said:**
> What GTK and Icon theme is that?  They're both really nice!

It is a modified version of nodoka squared, mixed with egtk's(elementary) nautilus code, and the icons are elementary.

Nodoka Squared's code is just changed so that the toolbar uses menubar gradient

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-10-12
> **armageddon08 said:**
> Another day, another brilliant piece of art by 8mil. Congrats. Care to share?

Thanks, but you are way too kind. As far as the screenshot goes, the wallpaper is [Down to Eternity by Daniel Laurini Jr]("http://www.flickr.com/photos/23959065@N06/3721291742/"). The color scheme is Obsidian Coast (Sunset). The widget style is Bespin. The plasma theme is Atelier. The icons are Oxygen Refit Black and the window decoration is Neon no buttons by FRUiT.

### Post by Twilight in Zero on 2009-10-14
Arch Linux. But you guys might be able to appreciate it a little more than the numerous terminal junkies on Arch's forums. ;) (nothing wrong with being a terminal junkie, though! :D)

XFCE + Compiz + gtk-window-decorator without gnome-control-center (and thus gnome-settings-daemon) dependency. :P

Icons are Gnome-colors, and GTK is a *heavily* modified Shiki-colors for roundedness and gloss (and because I detest thick tabs). Still experimenting with the gloss, though I think I'm content with it now. The color scheme is custom, I call it "Sublime." Font is DejaVu Sans Condensed (UME P Gothic S5 in my now playing conky). Wallpaper is right over here: [http://interfacelift.com/wallpaper_beta/details/2006/arch_tranquility.html](http://interfacelift.com/wallpaper_beta/details/2006/arch_tranquility.html)

In my conky, the outside two rings are the two CPU cores. The next one in is memory usage. The next one is my laptop battery. Top left inside is /. Top right inside is /home. Bottom inside is my Dad's Windows Vista partition.

Main conky config: [http://pastebin.com/f41466868](http://pastebin.com/f41466868)
Now playing (uses Quod Libet + its cover file plugin): [http://pastebin.com/f2de20fe1](http://pastebin.com/f2de20fe1)
rings.lua: [http://pastebin.com/fe01a24f](http://pastebin.com/fe01a24f)
gmail script: [http://pastebin.com/f3a8e9347](http://pastebin.com/f3a8e9347)

[[img]http://h.imagehost.org/t/0216/20091008-174528.jpg[/img]](http://h.imagehost.org/view/0216/20091008-174528) [[img]http://h.imagehost.org/t/0530/20091014-135140.jpg[/img]](http://h.imagehost.org/view/0530/20091014-135140)

---

Transparent right-click menu ? :o Hmm .. any chances to know how you achieved it ?

### Post by Twilight in Zero on 2009-10-14
> **Sarai the Geek said:**
> I usually despise glossiness (if that wasn't evident from my recent screenies :D) but that gtk theme looks awesome. Very nice work.
Yeah, Shiki-Colors isn't normally very glossy. It does have a little bit, but it's really subtle. My first modification was just to make the widgets rounded and a little bit more compact. The glossy one is separate in case I get tired of it. Thank you very much for your commendment! :)

> **OpenGuard said:**
> Transparent right-click menu ? :o Hmm .. any chances to know how you achieved it ?
I do it using Compiz, and all menus are translucent. The version I have has the opacity settings separated into a plugin: Opacity, Saturation, and Brightness. Older versions have opacity settings in General Settings, so adjust these instructions accordingly. Using CCSM, Enable that plugin, and add a rule in the Opacity tab. Set windows to "Menu | PopupMenu | DropdownMenu" and set the value to whatever opacity you want. 88 is good if you have blur, maybe 92 if not. If you have the Qt Window Fix enabled in Workarounds, disable it, or else certain fullscreen apps, like games, will become translucent too.

---

### Post by Sand &amp; Mercury on 2009-10-14
On this topic, I'd just like to point out that I've never ever seen any kind of Linux setup that successfully apes the look and feel of OS X down to a tee. The closest I've seen is Mac4Lin, which kind of gets close but ends up presenting nothing more than a very very obvious OS X knock-off.

The only platform where I've seen a really convincing attempt at aping the OS X look is on Windows XP of all places, like this: [http://sinedrock.deviantart.com/art/FInd-Your-Style-139000356](http://sinedrock.deviantart.com/art/FInd-Your-Style-139000356)

You can get almost-sort-of there in Linux but chucking in a dock, Lucida grande and GlobalMenu is not all it takes. There are so many elementary things that make Leopard look and feel distinct like its thin bar separators, the all-caps headers, the layout of the Finder application and the seamless integration of window decoration and GUI toolkit to name but a few, that simply cannot be emulated in Linux without extensive code modification to applications. 

I'm not really sure why I'm ranting about this but I just hope people don't do the whole 'Look it's OS X' thing on Linux thinking what they've made actually looks good. It's like foregoing the Giorgio Armani suit for the George Ormoni knock-off with loose seams and a gaudy stripe pattern on the insides, that is a lot cheaper for sure, and you might feel good wearing it but the emulation of the real deal falls right into the uncanny valley and looks REVOLTING.

Sorry. *Applies duct tape to mouth*

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-10-15
> **Mark76 said:**
> And where might I find these fonts?

More importantly. Are they open?

Sorry for the late reply.  Fontin can be found [here]("http://www.josbuivenga.demon.nl/fontin.html").  It isn't open-source, but it is free (gratis) and you are allowed to modify it as long as you do not sell or distribute the modification.  The full license information can be found on that site.  There are some really good fonts there besides Fontin, too.

Unfortunately for you, Franklin Gothic is both proprietary and commercial.  I don't even remember where *I *got it, but I do know I copied it over from my Windows partition.

---

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-10-16
> **eightmillion said:**
> Do all the rings in your clock represent different things or are the just an aesthetic touch?

No, they're all my stats, so from the innermost ring, going clockwise, it's hours, minutes, seconds, cpu1%, cpu2%, cpu total%, battery charge, mem%, day of the month, month and used drive space.  Whew.  Seems silly, but saves a lot of typing in my .conkyrc! :)

Oh, and goooorrrrrrggggeeeeeoooouuuuussss screenie.  The colour and the look is so rich.  I do miss KDE, but I don't miss it crashing my system all the time!

> **misfitpierce said:**
> I like it on the side too... It looks really nice :P - I have found that Gnome does not render panels on the side that great... Apparently KDE does not have any issues with this.
I think that if you just take the stock panel and put it on the side, then you'll have some problems. The task list generally doesn't look right and doesn't fit very many tasks. I'm using stasks in my screen shot so that only the icons are displayed. I think there's even a task list plasmoid that displays tasks names vertically for vertical panels. Also the default digital clock doesn't work very well in a vertical panel. In my screen shot I'm using the adjustable clock which allow formatting via html.

### Post by Amtal on 2009-10-16
> **raul_ said:**
> That allied with the lack of a decent Qt based browser can be quite frustrating (you know, because Firefox won't match the damn themes)

Arora isn't bad, but it just lacks features I use all the time in Firefox via extensions, namely Delicious and Evernote. I'm using the Delicious extension to keep all of my bookmarks in the cloud and replace the default bookmark system in Firefox. I use Evernote to keep recipes organized. Since I subscribe to a ton of food blog feeds, it's incredibly handy to only have to click one button to take a snapshot of recipe and add it to Evernote.

Oh, and I can't live without mouse gestures!

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-10-16
> **raul_ said:**
> That allied with the lack of a decent Qt based browser can be quite frustrating (you know, because Firefox won't match the damn themes)

Opera is Qt based, although you wouldn't necessarily know it by looking at it, and you have to go out of your way to find the [Qt4 version]("http://get.opera.com/pub/opera/linux/"). Also, Arora is pretty nice and I've heard good things about ReKonq although I haven't tried it.

> **Amtal said:**
> Oh, and I can't live without mouse gestures!

### Post by sertse on 2009-10-16
There is a Qt4 version. Opera just doesn't advertise it, and you need to get it directly from the mirror. Opera recommends the qt3 version. Even then, while it follows your theme (menus, colours, highlights etc), it uses it's own skin.

[http://ftp.opera.com/pub/opera/linux/1000/final/en/i386/](http://ftp.opera.com/pub/opera/linux/1000/final/en/i386/)

Not to mention Qt4 version is broken (hangs etc) atm on any Qt version past Qt 4.5.2 (e.g. 4.5.3).

### Post by raul_ on 2009-10-17
Ok, after the last discussion about Qt browsers I installed the git version of Rekonq, and I must say:

I take everything I said back. 

IMO rekonq currently is my browser of choice in KDE. It feels much more polished, renders pages properly (Flash websites, GMail with chat and everything), it has a "Chrome-like" home page (thumbnails of your favorites, history, etc) and it even has a smart url bar like Firefox.

Just awesome :)

### Post by raul_ on 2009-10-18
Daily rekonq .deb packages:

From PlanetKDE:

> I have seen that Rekonq is in the official karmic repository, than I decided to install it from there instead from sources. After the install, I have seen that was pretty buggy (mainly problems with cookies). With a quick research on google I found that the main developer (Andrea Diamantini) have fixed it in trunk. The result? I created the package on my ppa ([https://launchpad.net/~f4l3/+archive/ppa](https://launchpad.net/~f4l3/+archive/ppa)). I will recompile it every day ;), so if you want to join me using it... you are welcome ;).

Fabio Locati

> **armageddon08 said:**
> Beautiful screeny. Could you tell me how you got rid of the windec in terminal ? Also what is the terminal font?

Thanks. You can get rid of the border on Konsole by going to Window Behavior in System Settings and adding some rules for Konsole under window specific settings like this:

[IMG]http://omploader.org/vMmt4OA[/IMG]

The terminal font is [Inconsolata]("http://www.levien.com/type/myfonts/inconsolata.html").

### Post by dbbolton on 2009-10-21
> **etnlIcarus said:**
> Should use the same font for Gtk+, that you use for the openbox menu.

Most of the time (with TTF anyway) this is impossible. Openbox renders fonts differently than GTK. For example, if you set both to DejaVu Sans 8, the Openbox fonts will look a little smaller and not quite as smooth. I don't really know why, but that has been my experience.

---

### Post by etnlIcarus on 2009-10-21
> **dbbolton said:**
> Most of the time (with TTF anyway) this is impossible. Openbox renders fonts differently than GTK. For example, if you set both to DejaVu Sans 8, the Openbox fonts will look a little smaller and not quite as smooth. I don't really know why, but that has been my experience.

Probably because a) fonts are configured 10 different ways (I've found Qt4 apps and conky take ~/.fonts.conf's settings, over Xfce/Gnome's. Openbox is probably the same) and b) DPI settings are equally as unpredictable (had to force 96DPI in xserverrc, in .Xdefaults and in a couple of other places I can't recall).

The less said about getting consistent cursor themes, the better. Oy vey.

---

### Post by coldReactive on 2009-10-21
> **Mark76 said:**
> It's surprisingly easy.

So, what themes do you steal to customize for your own enjoyment? Also, HOW do you customize them, and HOW do we do it?

---

### Post by Mark76 on 2009-10-21
I just download and untar a theme directory from xfce-look.org, or copy one of the default xfwm themes available for Xubuntu, and then I copy an app(lication)run file from an original OroboROX theme and drop it in. That turns it into an executable app(lication) directory which I can run just by clicking on it.

Simple, no?

If I was more artistically inclined I'd make my own. OroboROX themes just use xpms. Which is why it's such a doddle to use xfwm ones.

---

### Post by Squonk07 on 2009-10-21
I became a convert to the "dark side" shortly after I posted last month's bluey theme. I absolutely love this combination, particularly the way the different levels of darkness play off one another. These screen shots should give you an idea what this theme looks like, as well as some of its limitations (the OO.org shot).

BTW, as you can see, I'm using Spatial Nautilus (as opposed to the default Browser behavior). You'd be surprised how usable it is once you know the keyboard shortcuts to stop all those extra windows from opening.

Theme: [Shiki-Colors]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=86717")
Wallpaper: [Gnome Darkwood]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php?content=102550")
Icons: Humanity (Ubuntu default)

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-10-25
> **Pott said:**
> How do you guys get so much customization on your desktop...? Is it easy to do? I wouldn't mind a dock and more window options...

It's not hard at all.

There's also plenty of Docks to choose from!

Cairo Dock
Avant Window Manager
Docky
Daisy (KDE only)


Those are just the ones I can think of from the top of my head. They're not hard to install either.

You can get themes from here:

[www.gnome-look.org](www.gnome-look.org)

or

[www.kde-look.org](www.kde-look.org)

Depending on what desktop environment you're using.

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-10-25
> **OpenGuard said:**

I want you to know that as I clicked "reply", I shifted my weight a bit (I'm lying in bed) and my laptop flew forward and whacked me right in the face. :P

Anyway...
OS: Crunchbang Linux
DE: Openbox
WM: [Arch.Blue]("http://www.box-look.org/content/show.php/arch.blue?content=74000") mod
GTK: [Elegant for Rent]("http://rent0n86.deviantart.com/art/Elegant-for-Rent-110013379") mod
ICONS: [allgrey]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/ALLGREY?content=76814"), [sketchy]("http://azuresol.deviantart.com/art/Sketchy-Icons-v-1-1-136712904"), [sketchy weather]("http://azuresol.deviantart.com/art/Sketchy-Weather-Icons-135079063")
FONTS: [artwiz's snap & nu]("http://sourceforge.net/projects/artwiz-latin1/"), [DIST Inking]("http://www.dafont.com/dist-inking.font")
CONKY: own design, inspiration from [vladislav]("http://arpinux.deviantart.com/art/vlasdislav-conky-setup-140402878")

GTK: [Elegant for Rent]("http://rent0n86.deviantart.com/art/Elegant-for-Rent-110013379") mod
ICONS: [allgrey]("http://www.gnome-look.org/content/show.php/ALLGREY?content=76814"), [sketchy]("http://azuresol.deviantart.com/art/Sketchy-Icons-v-1-1-136712904"), [sketchy weather]("http://azuresol.deviantart.com/art/Sketchy-Weather-Icons-135079063")
FONTS: [artwiz's snap & nu]("http://sourceforge.net/projects/artwiz-latin1/"), [DIST Inking]("http://www.dafont.com/dist-inking.font")
CONKY: own design, inspiration from [vladislav]("http://arpinux.deviantart.com/art/vlasdislav-conky-setup-140402878")

I don't have a link to the wallpaper- I forgot to fave it and don't really feel like scouring deviant art to find it again. If people want it, I can attach it.

Ouch! :D Thnx for the details - everything looks so perfect that I can't miss the chance to try it :)

### Post by Pott on 2009-10-25
Sorry guys but... what's Emerald or GTK...? I did some research on GTK but I can't figure much out, definitely not how to use it...

---

### Post by coldReactive on 2009-10-25
> **Pott said:**
> Sorry guys but... what's Emerald or GTK...? I did some research on GTK but I can't figure much out, definitely not how to use it...

GTK is a control decoration (so is QT), emerald is a window decorator. Metacity is also a Window Decorator.

---

### Post by Hetor on 2009-10-25
> **coldReactive said:**
> GTK is a control decoration (so is QT), emerald is a window decorator. Metacity is also a Window Decorator.

Actually, metacity is not a decorator but a window manager. And GTK is a widget toolkit.

---

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-10-25
> **Hetor said:**
> Actually, metacity is not a decorator but a window manager. And GTK is a widget toolkit.

Let's not confuse him now, he's a beginner (Pott).

---

### Post by misfitpierce on 2009-10-25
> **Pott said:**
> Sorry guys but... what's Emerald or GTK...? I did some research on GTK but I can't figure much out, definitely not how to use it...

Ok go to [http://gnome-look.org](http://gnome-look.org) and for themes you want to color the window you select GTK 2.0 on left side, for window borders you select metacity although some GTK creations come with window borders as well unless otherwise stated, and for icons... of course you hit icons...

 Now... when you download the file should be a .tar.gz file that you can put somewhere on computer aka under Documents or something... If it is not .tar.gz try opening the archive and seeing if .tar.gz is inside. Once you place the .tar.gz theme file whether it be icons, metacity or GTK theme somewhere on computer that you can remember go to System -- Pref -- Appearance where the themes are and hit install and then select the .tar.gz wherever it is.

If need more help just ask but thats a quick laydown of what they are and how to install them... Its quite easy once you get the hang of it!

---

### Post by SomeGuyDude on 2009-10-25
> **Pott said:**
> Sorry guys but... what's Emerald or GTK...? I did some research on GTK but I can't figure much out, definitely not how to use it...

Imagining your windows are paintings, Emerald is a kind of frame for it, and GTK is what's used to paint the painting itself.

Midori is definitely GTK based and does work with the globalmenu plugin. I chose it because it's going to be the default browser for xfce4 and I'm trying to use xfce4 components as much as possible (although some Gnome panel plugins are a better fit for the OS X look).

And talking of gnome-panel applets. Does anyone know why there isn't one for volume control? The Xfce4 one is disappointingly ugly.

Have no shame using Midori! :) I use it as my main browser even and it's awesome. They putting some really nice things in..

The gnome volume control is part of the package "gnome-applets" containing all the default gnome panel plugins. Unfortunately it brings in a lot of stuff:

The following NEW packages will be installed:
  capplets-data evolution-data-server-common gnome-about gnome-applets gnome-applets-data gnome-control-center
  gnome-desktop-data gnome-menus gnome-panel gnome-panel-data gnome-settings-daemon libapm1 libcpufreq0 libecal1.2-7
  libedataserverui1.2-8 libgnome-menu2 libgnome-window-settings1 libgnomekbd-common libgnomekbd4 libgucharmap7

  metacity-common python-gmenu system-tools-backends

### Post by londonali1010 on 2009-10-27
> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> that analog clock is conky? if so, i need you to teach me how to do that.

:)

It's done with a Lua script called from Conky, using Cairo bindings for Lua. The Conky Blog has a ["getting started" guide]("http://blog.conky.be/2009/09/28/lua-cairo-bindings-getting-started/"), and you can get my widgets script and some widget code blocks over at [Conky Hardcore!]("http://conky.linux-hardcore.com/?page_id=3331")

There's also loads more going on on the [Conky thread]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showthread.php?t=281865") here, which has just ticked over 10,000 posts!!!

---

### Post by chucky chuckaluck on 2009-10-27
> **londonali1010 said:**
> :)

It's done with a Lua script called from Conky, using Cairo bindings for Lua. The Conky Blog has a ["getting started" guide]("http://blog.conky.be/2009/09/28/lua-cairo-bindings-getting-started/"), and you can get my widgets script and some widget code blocks over at [Conky Hardcore!]("http://conky.linux-hardcore.com/?page_id=3331")

### Post by applecake on 2009-10-27
> **Pott said:**
> Hey guys quick question... I'd like to mess around with a good looking, easy to use dock and a simple Conky with something like calendar, CPU/RAM usage and an analogue clock. I tried sudo apt-get install Docky but to no avail. I can't figure out how to install the darn things! They're not in the add/remove applications...

Thanks!

I presume you are talking about Gnome Do Docky? Docky is a part of the Gnome Do, so search for Gnome Do in Add/Remove 
Applications. Then, when it starts, right click (I think, or click on the arrow in upper right corner), and choose "Properties". Then, under Appeareance tab, choose the theme Docky.
I don't know about Conky though..
Hope this helps some.. I'm currently not in Ubuntu.. :(

---

### Post by Tibuda on 2009-10-27

Currently they are the same app, but they will split on the next releases.

### Post by RiceMonster on 2009-10-27
> **Felliph3 said:**
> Looks good, care to tell me more about the deskspace applet?( One,two,three,four)
Can I get that in Gnome?

You can do that in GNOME. Right click on the pager, do to preferences, then click "show names of work spaces" or something like that. Make sure you name your workspaces One, Two, Three, Four, etc. etnlIcarus is basically doing the same thing with Xfce panel.

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-10-27
There have been lots of great screenshots over the past several days. This is my first shot from Karmic Koala.

[[IMG]http://omploader.org/vMm14dQ[/IMG]]("http://omploader.org/vMm14dA")

    I have to say that for me, Karmic is the best Ubuntu release yet, and I've been using Ubuntu since Warty. Everything just works. I don't even have to use ndiswrapper any longer. The only thing that I had to do after installing was the removal of pulse audio. It's an especially stark contrast coming from Jaunty, which I consider to be the worst Ubuntu release (I might as well have been running Linux From Scratch). 

    The upgrade from Jaunty was not smooth though. I was prompted to reboot too soon, before udev was configured, resulting in an unbootable installation. I tried booting a live cd, chrooting to my hard drive, and reconfiguring udev, but that didn't work, so I resized my old root partition and used it as the home partition for my new install (the new Kubuntu installer is very slick).

tl;dr Jaunty was a dog's breakfast and Karmic is the dog's dinner.

---

### Post by the fix it man on 2009-10-27
> **eightmillion said:**
> There have been lots of great screenshots over the past several days. This is my first shot from Karmic Koala.

[[IMG]http://omploader.org/vMm14dQ[/IMG]]("http://omploader.org/vMm14dA")

    I have to say that for me, Karmic is the best Ubuntu release yet, and I've been using Ubuntu since Warty. Everything just works. I don't even have to use ndiswrapper any longer. The only thing that I had to do after installing was the removal of pulse audio. It's an especially stark contrast coming from Jaunty, which I consider to be the worst Ubuntu release (I might as well have been running Linux From Scratch). 

    The upgrade from Jaunty was not smooth though. I was prompted to reboot too soon, before udev was configured, resulting in an unbootable installation. I tried booting a live cd, chrooting to my hard drive, and reconfiguring udev, but that didn't work, so I resized my old root partition and used it as the home partition for my new install (the new Kubuntu installer is very slick).

tl;dr Jaunty was a dog's breakfast and Karmic is the dog's dinner.

Great desktop~
Pretty much echo your experience here, although to be fair with Jaunty the Ubuntu team did'nt have much to work with on kde4.0.

The last year or so I have been going back and forth from Gnome, KDe, Xfce mainly trying to find the best combo with for rendering speed for web browsers and could never settle with FF on any platform, now I have discovered opera in KDE 4.3.2 :D

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-10-27
> **the fix it man said:**
> Great desktop~
Pretty much echo your experience here, although to be fair with Jaunty the Ubuntu team did'nt have much to work with on kde4.0.

The last year or so I have been going back and forth from Gnome, KDe, Xfce mainly trying to find the best combo with for rendering speed for web browsers and could never settle with FF on any platform, now I have discovered opera in KDE 4.3.2 :D

Thanks. My problem was never with KDE. It was with drivers and stability. I have an Intel graphics card. I never did get that to work correctly, even though I was upgrading drivers and kernels all the time. The performance sucked and about once a day the display would grind to halt, and thrash the hard disk for some reason that I never did figure out and I'd have to restart X. Then ndiswrapper had some kind of bug with my setup where it would segfault pretty routinely. I ended up writing a program to watch the module and remove it, then reinsert it whenever it would crash. Every once in a while that would cause a kernel panic. I had read that the Intel performance was better with kernel 2.6.31, but I never could get ndiswrapper to compile against 2.6.31, so that was a catch 22. As far as I know, the svn version of ndiswrapper still won't compile against 2.6.31 without modification.

Jaunty was a giant pain in the ***. ](*,)

### Post by gjoellee on 2009-10-28
> No, but mine is! [http://conky.linux-hardcore.com/?page_id=2800](http://conky.linux-hardcore.com/?page_id=2800) :wink: :grin:

> **chucky chuckaluck said:**
> ooh, i like that. is your .conkyrc around somewhere?

conkyrc:
```
# -- Conky settings -- #
background no
update_interval 1
 
cpu_avg_samples 2
net_avg_samples 2
 
override_utf8_locale yes
 
double_buffer yes
no_buffers yes
 
text_buffer_size 2048
imlib_cache_size 0
 
# -- Window specifications -- #
 
own_window yes
own_window_type desktop
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorate,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager,below
 
border_inner_margin 0
border_outer_margin 0
 
minimum_size 1020 600
maximum_width 1000
 
alignment tm
gap_x 10
gap_y 0
 
# -- Graphics settings -- #
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
 
# -- Text settings -- #
use_xft yes
xftfont Santana:size=24
xftalpha 0.8
 
uppercase no
 
default_color FFFFFF
 
# -- Lua Load -- #
lua_load ~/.clock_mod.lua
lua_draw_hook_pre ring_stats
 
TEXT
${voffset 35}${font Santana:size=50}${alignr}${time %H.%M}${font}
${goto 160}${hr 2}
${goto 250}${time %A, %d %B %Y}

```clock_mod.lua:
```
--[[
Ring Meters by londonali1010 (2009)
 
This script draws percentage meters as rings. It is fully customisable; all options are described in the script.
 
IMPORTANT: if you are using the 'cpu' function, it will cause a segmentation fault if it tries to draw a ring straight away. The if statement on line 145 uses a delay to make sure that this doesn't happen. It calculates the length of the delay by the number of updates since Conky started. Generally, a value of 5s is long enough, so if you update Conky every 1s, use update_num > 5 in that if statement (the default). If you only update Conky every 2s, you should change it to update_num > 3; conversely if you update Conky every 0.5s, you should use update_num > 10. ALSO, if you change your Conky, is it best to use "killall conky; conky" to update it, otherwise the update_num will not be reset and you will get an error.
 
To call this script in Conky, use the following (assuming that you save this script to ~/scripts/rings.lua):
    lua_load ~/scripts/rings-v1.2.1.lua
    lua_draw_hook_pre ring_stats
 
Changelog:
+ v1.2.1 -- Fixed minor bug that caused script to crash if conky_parse() returns a nil value (20.10.2009)
+ v1.2 -- Added option for the ending angle of the rings (07.10.2009)
+ v1.1 -- Added options for the starting angle of the rings, and added the "max" variable, to allow for variables that output a numerical value rather than a percentage (29.09.2009)
+ v1.0 -- Original release (28.09.2009)
]]
 
settings_table = {
    {
        -- Edit this table to customise your rings.
        -- You can create more rings simply by adding more elements to settings_table.
        -- "name" is the type of stat to display; you can choose from 'cpu', 'memperc', 'fs_used_perc', 'battery_used_perc'.
        name='time',
        -- "arg" is the argument to the stat type, e.g. if in Conky you would write ${cpu cpu0}, 'cpu0' would be the argument. If you would not use an argument in the Conky variable, use ''.
        arg='%I.%M',
        -- "max" is the maximum value of the ring. If the Conky variable outputs a percentage, use 100.
        max=12,
        -- "bg_colour" is the colour of the base ring.
        bg_colour=0xffffff,
        -- "bg_alpha" is the alpha value of the base ring.
        bg_alpha=0.1,
        -- "fg_colour" is the colour of the indicator part of the ring.
        fg_colour=0xffffff,
        -- "fg_alpha" is the alpha value of the indicator part of the ring.
        fg_alpha=0.2,
        -- "x" and "y" are the x and y coordinates of the centre of the ring, relative to the top left corner of the Conky window.
        x=165, y=170,
        -- "radius" is the radius of the ring.
        radius=50,
        -- "thickness" is the thickness of the ring, centred around the radius.
        thickness=5,
        -- "start_angle" is the starting angle of the ring, in degrees, clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative.
        start_angle=0,
        -- "end_angle" is the ending angle of the ring, in degrees, clockwise from top. Value can be either positive or negative, but must be larger (e.g. more clockwise) than start_angle.
        end_angle=360
    },
    {
        name='time',
        arg='%M.%S',
        max=60,
        bg_colour=0xffffff,
        bg_alpha=0.1,
        fg_colour=0xffffff,
        fg_alpha=0.4,
        x=165, y=170,
        radius=56,
        thickness=5,
        start_angle=0,
        end_angle=360
    },
    {
        name='time',
        arg='%S',
        max=60,
        bg_colour=0xffffff,
        bg_alpha=0.1,
        fg_colour=0xffffff,
        fg_alpha=0.6,
        x=165, y=170,
        radius=62,
        thickness=5,
        start_angle=0,
        end_angle=360
    },
    {
        name='cpu',
        arg='cpu1',
        max=100,
        bg_colour=0xffffff,
        bg_alpha=0,
        fg_colour=0xffffff,
        fg_alpha=0.1,
        x=165, y=170,
        radius=70,
        thickness=5,
        start_angle=60,
        end_angle=120
    },
    {
        name='cpu',
        arg='cpu0',
        max=100,
        bg_colour=0xffffff,
        bg_alpha=0.1,
        fg_colour=0xffffff,
        fg_alpha=0.4,
        x=165, y=170,
        radius=84.5,
        thickness=8,
        start_angle=60,
        end_angle=120
    },
    {
        name='memperc',
        arg='',
        max=100,
        bg_colour=0xffffff,
        bg_alpha=0.1,
        fg_colour=0xffffff,
        fg_alpha=0.8,
        x=165, y=170,
        radius=83.5,
        thickness=8,
        start_angle=122,
        end_angle=210
    },
    {
        name='time',
        arg='%d',
        max=31,
        bg_colour=0xffffff,
        bg_alpha=0.1,
        fg_colour=0xffffff,
        fg_alpha=0.8,
        x=165, y=170,
        radius=70,
        thickness=5,
        start_angle=212,
        end_angle=360
    },
    {
        name='time',
        arg='%m',
        max=12,
        bg_colour=0xffffff,
        bg_alpha=0.1,
        fg_colour=0xffffff,
        fg_alpha=0.8,
        x=165, y=170,
        radius=76,
        thickness=5,
        start_angle=212,
        end_angle=360
    },
    {
        name='fs_used_perc',
        arg='/',
        max=150,
        bg_colour=0xffffff,
        bg_alpha=0.2,
        fg_colour=0xffffff,
        fg_alpha=0.3,
        x=165, y=170,
        radius=108.5,
        thickness=3,
        start_angle=-120,
        end_angle=240
    },
    {
        name='fs_used_perc',
        arg='/',
        max=100,
        bg_colour=0xffffff,
        bg_alpha=0.2,
        fg_colour=0xffffff,
        fg_alpha=0.3,
        x=165, y=170,
        radius=135,
        thickness=50,
        start_angle=-120,
        end_angle=120
    },
}
 
require 'cairo'
 
function rgb_to_r_g_b(colour,alpha)
    return ((colour / 0x10000) % 0x100) / 255., ((colour / 0x100) % 0x100) / 255., (colour % 0x100) / 255., alpha
end
 
function draw_ring(cr,t,pt)
    local w,h=conky_window.width,conky_window.height
 
    local xc,yc,ring_r,ring_w,sa,ea=pt['x'],pt['y'],pt['radius'],pt['thickness'],pt['start_angle'],pt['end_angle']
    local bgc, bga, fgc, fga=pt['bg_colour'], pt['bg_alpha'], pt['fg_colour'], pt['fg_alpha']
 
    local angle_0=sa*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
    local angle_f=ea*(2*math.pi/360)-math.pi/2
    local t_arc=t*(angle_f-angle_0)
 
    -- Draw background ring
 
    cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,ring_r,angle_0,angle_f)
    cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(bgc,bga))
    cairo_set_line_width(cr,ring_w)
    cairo_stroke(cr)
 
    -- Draw indicator ring
 
    cairo_arc(cr,xc,yc,ring_r,angle_0,angle_0+t_arc)
    cairo_set_source_rgba(cr,rgb_to_r_g_b(fgc,fga))
    cairo_stroke(cr)        
end
 
function conky_ring_stats()
    local function setup_rings(cr,pt)
        local str=''
        local value=0
 
        str=string.format('${%s %s}',pt['name'],pt['arg'])
        str=conky_parse(str)
 
        value=tonumber(str)
        if value == nil then value = 0 end
        pct=value/pt['max']
 
        draw_ring(cr,pct,pt)
    end
 
    if conky_window==nil then return end
    local cs=cairo_xlib_surface_create(conky_window.display,conky_window.drawable,conky_window.visual, conky_window.width,conky_window.height)
 
    local cr=cairo_create(cs)    
 
    local updates=conky_parse('${updates}')
    update_num=tonumber(updates)
 
    if update_num>5 then
        for i in pairs(settings_table) do
            setup_rings(cr,settings_table[i])
        end
    end
end

```

For those who does not understand how to get my conky:

2. If you open the /usr/share/icons folder you'll see many folders with your icon themes. Copy the theme you want as a base to /home/username/.icons and start changing your icons with your image editor.

3. The network manager sits on the notification area. You have to move the full area, you can't move only one icon.

4. It is a customizable system monitor that can do almost anything.

5. What is "the clear launcher type thing"?

### Post by tehkain on 2009-10-28
> **tehkain said:**
> [[IMG]http://imgur.com/GAV9Yl.png[/IMG]](http://imgur.com/GAV9Y.png)
Hey guys, thanks for the praise. We will start with the panel, first off it is just one panel. I used a full screen width background that is transparent in the center, and then I disabled the panels shadow. After that I patched the window picker applet and notification area applet to have more padding, and to use icons 3px smaller than the panel size. I also made the handles transparent.

As for the globalmenu, someone mentioned earlier that banshee's compact mode does have any menus and they were correct. So just imagine a full menu bar there.

Now onto the my theme, getting nautilus to look like that is tricky but you can use the code/images from the Elementary gtk theme to implement this in any theme. My theme is Nodoka Squared with font modifications, toolbar changes, and highlight fixes. I will look into putting it on gnome-look as soon as I get a chance to work out the licensing issues.

edit: Oh this is Karmic by the way, my Gutsy Gibbon Testing note is not to be believed.

---

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-10-29
> **londonali1010 said:**
> Hm. How old do you think I am? Wait. Don't answer that.

My first computer was actually a tiny old Macintosh with about a 6" screen, black and white, and a little floppy drive. I used to play the text version of The Hitchhikers' Guide to the Galaxy, and my house always got bulldozed :)

And I do remember distinctly changing the "wallpaper" on that, some horrible pixelated black and white pattern options were all I had, but ahhhh...I was into desktop customisation even back at the age of 7. :KS
I don't remember what my first computer was, exactly, but I remember that it was CLI and I would sit there for hours doing something like this:

```

C:\\ DOES THIS DO ANYTHING
DOES THIS DO ANYTHING: Command not found

C:\\ PLEASE JUST DO SOMETHING!!
PLEASE JUST DO SOMETHING!!: Command not found

```
It had an amber screen and all I could ever get it to do was play the Alaska state anthem.

That said, it was very obsolete even at the time and my dad just had a thing for old computers. I think the first operating system I recall clearly was Windows 3.1... and yes, I used the Hot Dog Stand theme!

[[img]http://ubuntu-pics.de/thumb/29203/mlk_oQQD6J.png[/img]](http://ubuntu-pics.de/bild/29203/mlk_oQQD6J.png) [[img]http://ubuntu-pics.de/thumb/29204/mlk1_fQBbYd.png[/img]](http://ubuntu-pics.de/bild/29204/mlk1_fQBbYd.png) [[img]http://ubuntu-pics.de/thumb/29205/mlk2_eOHHUG.png[/img]](http://ubuntu-pics.de/bild/29205/mlk2_eOHHUG.png)

Bit late, I know but I hadn't noticed the rounded/cropped corners on the progress bars, in your previous shots. Gtk+ and rounded progress bars do not mix, primarily because the progress 'frame' does not support rounded edges. It looks doubly bad when a progress bar is embedded into a list/treeview.
